Jamison Brereton

191
Against Poisonous Animals
Agastya Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
16 verses: anuс╣гс╣нubh, except mah─Бpaс╣Еkti 10тАУ12, mah─Бbr╠еhat─л 13
Very Atharvan in style, this hymn, directed against stinging and poisonous insects, does indeed have a number of parallels and near-parallels in the Atharvaveda. Like that text, it frequently uses expressions of the immediate past (especially in the aor ist) as a triumphant predictor of successful measures taken in the present. That is, a statement like тАЬthey have been wiped outтАЭ (vs. 1d), though apparently referring to the past, probably instead announces, hopefully, that the current verbal spell along with whatever physical magic practices have been undertaken will ensure that the desired effect will have happened this instant. Unfortunately we have no real idea what the physical rites involved, though judging from parallels like Atharvaveda VII.56, entitled by Whitney тАЬAgainst poison of snakes and insects,тАЭ it may well have involved healing plants and insect-eating birds.
The first nine verses of the hymn are directed particularly against adr╠е╠Бс╣гtaтАФтАЬthe unseen, invisibleтАЭтАФapparently small biting insects. English has a remarkably close counterpart in the colloquially named тАЬno-see-ums,тАЭ which also share behaviors with their Sanskrit counterparts: clinging to grasses (vs. 3) and becoming especially virulent in the early evening (vss. 4тАУ5). And anyone who has ever attempted to swat a flying bug ruefully recognizes the commands given in verse 6: тАЬstand still! come to rest!тАЭ
In the rest of the hymn (vss. 10тАУ16) the speaker works to render ineffective and harmless the poison of poisonous insects more generally. One of the most salient features of this part of the hymn is the density of diminutivization, that is, of the use of the colloquial, low-register -ka-suffix, which appears not only on nouns referring to bugs and birds, but also on pronouns and demonstrative adjectives (vss. 11, 15) and even on a participle (vs. 16). (For further on the sociolinguistics of the -ka-suffix, see Jamison 2009b). Though for the most part the tools deployed against the poison are homely onesтАФlittle birds and plants, insofar as we can tellтАФthis section of the hymn begins with higher rhetorical ambitions and a mythic model. In verse 10, whose interpretation is much disputed, the speaker fastens the poison on the sun and the skin containing the poison (in our view) тАЬon the house of the possessor of liquor (sur─Б).тАЭ Although most commentators, beginning at least with S─Бyaс╣Зa, interpret the latter action as an unmarked simile likening this action to the fastening of the poison on the sun, in our view it is a parallel mytho-ritual action and provides the mythic model for the ritual actions that follow. Again in our view, the possessor of liquor is IndraтАФa reference to a myth well known in the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas and already clearly present in the late R╠еgveda (X.131.4тАУ5), in which Indra, sickened from drinking an excess of soma, is made to drink the usually for bidden alcohol sur─Б by the A┼Ыvins and Sarasvat─л. The sur─Б was not pure but mixed, and both the A┼Ыvins and Indra perform the singular feat of separating the two mixed liquids in the course of drinking themтАФa detail found in the R╠еgvedic treat ment just cited. The ability to separate liquids, to get rid of (or nullify the effects of) the noxious one and preserve the beneficial one, is what the ritual performer desires here, as the last two p─Бdas of the refrain (vss. 10тАУ13ef) make clear.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Against poisonous animals Because of the popular character of this hymn and the idiomatic specificity of the entities mentioned, much of the vocabulary is obscure. I will not discuss the supposed real-world identifications or etymological speculations for each lexical item. Reasonably up-to-date treatments of the sec. lit. are available in EWA, s.vv.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSome creature of little venom, some creature of great venom; or some venomous aquatic reptile; creatures of two kinds, both destructive (of life),or (poisonous) unseen creatures, have anointed me with their poison.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The s┼лkta is a mystical antidote against poison. This was recited by Agastya under an apprehension of having been poisoned. kaс╣Еkata, na kaс╣Еkata, sat─лna kaс╣Еkata = alpaviс╣гaс╕е kas;cit, something of little venom; tadvipar─лto analpaviс╣гo mahorag─Бi, the opposite of that of not little venom, like great snakes and the like;

Satina = water; of two kinds: of little or of much venom; or creatures of land or water; unseen creatures: adс╣Ыс╣гс╣н─Б = of invisible forms; the appellation of certain poisonous insects; a class of poisons, or of poisonous creatures: vi┼Ыavi┼Ыeс╣гaс╕е viс╣гadhara vi┼Ыeс╣гa v─Б; having anointed: alipsata = have smeared, have spread over all the limbs

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╡рд┐рд╖реМрд╖рдзрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╡реИрджреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдХрдЩреНрдХрддрдГ) рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╡рд╛рдиреН (рди) рдЗрд╡ (рдХрдЩреНрдХрддрдГ) рдЪрдЮреНрдЪрд▓рдГ (рдЕрдереЛ) рдЖрдирдиреНрддрд░реНрдпреЗ (рд╕рддреАрдирдХрдЩреНрдХрддрдГ) рд╕рддреАрдирдорд┐рд╡ рдЪрдЮреНрдЪрд▓рдГред рд╕рддреАрдирдорд┐рддреНрдпреБрджрдХрдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрдореН ред рдирд┐рдШрдВреж резред резреиред (рджреНрд╡реМ) (рдЗрддрд┐) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░реЗ (рдкреНрд▓реБрд╖реА рдЗрддрд┐) рджрд╛рд╣рдХреМ рджреБрдГрдЦрдкреНрд░рджреМ (рдирд┐) (рдЕрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдГ) рдпреЗрди рджреГрд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рддреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдзрд╛рд░рд┐рдгреЛ рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рдГ (рдЕрд▓рд┐рдкреНрд╕рдд) рд▓рд┐рдореНрдкрдиреНрддрд┐ рее рез рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░рдГред рдпрдерд╛ рдХрд╢реНрдЪреНрдЪрд┐рдЪреНрдЪрдЮреНрдЪрд▓реЛ рдЬрдиреЛрд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрдкрджреЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░реМ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдп рдХрдЩреНрдХрддреЗ рддрдерд╛рд╜рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдзрд╛рд░рд┐рдгрдГ рдХреНрд╖реБрджреНрд░рд╛ рдЬреАрд╡рд╛рдГ рдкреБрдирдГ рдкреБрдирд░реНрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рд┐рддрд╛ рдЕрдкреНрдпреБрдкрд░рд┐ рдкрддрдиреНрддрд┐ рее рез рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(the antidote), coming (to the bitten person n), destroys the unseen (venomous creatures); departing (it destroys them); deprived (of substance), it destroys them (by its odour); being ground, it pulverises them.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Deprives of substance: avaghnat─л = avahanyam─Бnaauс╣гadhiс╕е, a drug or antidote being destroyed; losing its substance, and reduced to its odour; or it may mean that a certain drug,understood, is destructive of poisonous creatures

Jamison Brereton

As she comes, she smashes the no-see-ums, and as she goes away, she smashes them.
Smashing them down, she smashes them, and crushing, she
crushes them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The feminine nemesis is not identified. As Geldner notes (n. 2), S─Бyaс╣Зa. suggests itтАЩs the healing plant, Henry both the plant and dawn.

Griffith

Coming, it kills the unobserved; it kills them as it goes away,
It kills them as it drives them off, and bruising bruises them to death.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Blades of) ┼Ыar─Б grass, (of) ku┼Ыar─Б, (of) darbha, (of) sairy─Б, (of) mu├▒ja, (of) v─лraс╣Зa, all (the haunt) of unseen (venomous creatures), have together anointed me (with their venom).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Blades of ┼Ыar─Б: these are, saccarum ┼Ыara, poa cynosuroides, saccharum spontaneum, saccarum mu├▒ja, andropogon muricatum, long-reed like grasses, amidst which reptiles may lurk unseen

Jamison Brereton

The reeds and the damn reeds, the darbha-grasses and (the bugs) on the sira-plants [?],
the no-see-ums on the mu├▒ja-grass and on the v─лraс╣Зa-grassтАФall have been wiped out at once.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take k├║┼Ыara- as containing the pejorative ku-prefix (as in k├║-yava- тАШ(bringing) bad harvestтАЩ) and a play on the preceding word ┼Ыar├б-.

The three vс╣Ыddhi derivatives, sairy├б-, mau├▒j├б-, and vairiс╣З├б-, I interpret flg.

S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs suggestion for the last two, namely that they refer to the adс╣Ы╠Бс╣гta- bugs found on those particular grasses. Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe cows had lain down in their stalls; the wild beasts had retreated (to their lairs); the senses of men were at rest; when the unseen (venomous creatures) anointed me (with their venom).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The unseen venomous creatures: these reptiles being most frequent at night or in the dark

Jamison Brereton

The cows have sat down in the cowshed; the wild animals have settled downтАФ
down (also) the lights of the peoples. The no-see-ums have been
wiped out.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. seems an attempt at sympathetic magic: animals, both domestic and wild, and humans (symbolized by their lights, presumably their fires) are all settling down for the night (though the time period is not explicit), and so should the bugs.

As anyone whoтАЩs ever been outside in a buggy place after dark knows, this magic is not necessarily going to work – though itтАЩs true that some types of bugs are active at dusk and then stop.

Griffith

The cows had settled in their stalls, the beasts of prey had sought their lairs,
Extinguished were the lights of men, when things unseen infected me.

Geldner

Die K├╝he haben sich im Stall niedergelegt, das Wild ist zur Ruhe gegangen, zur Ruhe auch die Lichter des Menschen, die Unsichtbaren sind angeschmiert.

Grassmann

Die K├╝he haben sich in ihrem Stall niedergelassen, die Waldthiere sind eingekehrt, die Lichter der Menschen [sind erloschen], und das unbemerkte Gew├╝rm ist verschwunden.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬOr they may be discovered (in the dark), as thieves in the (dusk of) evening; for although they be unseen, yet all are seen by them; therefore, men, be vigilant.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Discovered in the dark: as snakes by their breathing; yet all are seen by them: vi┼Ыvadс╣Ыс╣гс╣н─Б, undertood it as a bahuvr─лhi compound

Jamison Brereton

And these very ones have come into sight in the early evening, like thieves.
You no-see-ums seen by all, you have become recognized.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. does seem to refer to such insects, those that become active at twilight when the wind drops. For example, although there are numerous types of mosquitoes and different species have different feeding patterns, it seems (from a quick Google search) that most species feed at dawn and dusk and a few hours into the dark.

Griffith

Or these, these reptiles, are observed, like lurking thieves at evening time.
Seers of all, themselves unseen: be therefore very vigilant.

Geldner

Diese sind wieder erschienen bei Anbruch des Dunkels wie die Diebe. Ihr Unsichtbaren seid allgesehen, erkannt worden.

Grassmann

Und diese sind in der Nacht wieder sichtbar geworden, wie Diebe, ihr unbemerkten Gew├╝rme seid von allen bemerkt und wahrgenommen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬHeaven, (serpents), is your father; Earth, your mother; Soma, your brother; Aditi, your sister; unseen all-seeing abide (in your own holes); enjoy (your own) good plural asure.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Soma is here the moon; heaven is the residence of Soma: somadharo dyulokaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Your father is Heaven, and your mother the Earth. Your brother is Soma, and your sister Aditi.
You no-see-ums seen by all, stand still! come to rest!

Jamison Brereton Notes

It is unclear to me why the bugs are being credited with such a grand pedigree. Perhaps to indicate that they are ubiquitous in the space between earth and heaven? S─Бyaс╣Зa. suggests this vs. and the next are addressed to snakes, but there seems no reason why adс╣Ы╠Бс╣гta- would change its referent. As I noted in the published introduction, the impulse to demand that a troublesome unswattable bug settle down long enough to be squashed is likely to be universal.

Griffith

Heaven is your Sire, your Mother Earth, Soma your Brother, Aditi
Your Sister: seeing all, unseen, keep still and dwell ye happily.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThose (who move with their) shoulders, those (who move with their) bodies, those who sting with sharp fangs, those who are virulently venomous; what do you here, you unseen, depart together far from us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Those who move: ye aс╣Гsy─Б ye aс╣Еgy─Бс╕е, what relates to the shoulders, or the body genitive rally;

Aс╣Гsy─Б = being suited to the shoulders, moving with or by them, born or produced in or on them, biting with them: aс╣Гs─Бrh─Бс╕е, aс╣Гsag─Бс╕е, aс╣Гse bhav─Бс╕е, aс╣Гs─Бbhy─Бm kh─Бdantaс╕е;

Aс╣Гgy─Б = moving with the body or poisoning with the body, as certain spiders, whose contact is poisonous, and the like; who stings with sharp fangs: suc─лk─Бс╕е, having sharp needle-like stings, like a scorpion

Jamison Brereton

The ones on (my) shoulders, the ones on (my) limbs, the little needle bugs with their stingers outтАФ
you no-see-ums, there is nothing at all for you here. All of you, get worn down at once!

Griffith

Biters of shoulder or of limb, with needle-stings, most venomous,
Unseen, whatever ye may be, vanish together and be gone.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe all-seeing Sun rises in the east, the destroyer of the unseen, driving away all the unseen (venomous creatures), and all evil spirits.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Destroyer of the unseen: adс╣Ыс╣гс╣нh─Б may also mean the dissipator of darkness; adс╣Ыс╣гс╣нa occurs in the sense of invisible venomous creatures, these as well as the y─Бtudh─Бnas, or r─Бkс╣гasas, disappear at sunrise; cf. AV 5.23.6

Jamison Brereton Notes

The rising of the sun may reflect the fact, mentioned above, that many bugs feed at twilight (dawn and dusk), and sunrise portends the end of the (pre-)dawn feeding frenzy.

Consuming all that are not seen, and evil spirits of the night.

English translation:

тАЬThe Sun has risen on high, destroying all the many (poisons); ─Аditya, the all-seeing, the destroyer of the unseen, (rises) for (the good of) living beings.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Up has flown yonder Sun, incinerating all the manyтАФ
the ─Аditya (up) from the mountains, the smasher of the no-see-ums, seen by all. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The rising of the sun may reflect the fact, mentioned above, that many bugs feed at twilight (dawn and dusk), and sunrise portends the end of the (pre-)dawn feeding frenzy.

Griffith

There hath the Sun-God mounted up, who scorches much and everything.
Even the Aditya from the hills, all-seen, destroying things unseen.

Geldner

Emporgeflogen ist dort der Sonnengott, vielfach alles versengend, der Aditja vom Berge herab von allen bemerkt, t├╢dtend das unbemerkte Gew├╝rm.

рее рее резрел рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI deposit the poison in the solar orb, like a leather bottle in the house of a vendor of spirits; verily, that adorable (Sun) never dies; nor, (through his favour), shall we die (of the venom); for, though afar off, yet drawn by his coursers, he will overtake (the poison); the science of antidoes converted you, (Poison), to ambrosia.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This and the following three hymns are derived from the viс╣гa vidy─Б, the science of poisons,or of antidoes, whence it is also termed madhu-vidy─Б, science of ambrosia; ‘having taken the poison in the solar orb with the fourth finger, having made it ambrosia and caused them to blend together, may it become poisonless’; s┼лrya maс╣Зс╕Нala or orb of the sun; or, perhaps a reference to a mystical diagram or figure typical of the solar orb;

Madhuta = madhu vidy─Б was originally taught by Indra to Dadhya├▒c, who communicated it to the A┼Ыvins, and thereby lost his head

Jamison Brereton

I fasten the poison on the Sun, the skin (containing it) on the house of the possessor of liquor [=Indra].
Even now he will not die, and we will not die.
The mounter of the fallow bays [=Indra] has (made) its [=poisonтАЩs] trek far in the distance; the honeyed (plant) has made you honey.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, the second part of the hymn begins here, but it clearly pivots on the sun, which figured in the two preceding vss.

My interpr. of this much discussed vs. is presented in the published introduction, but in compressed fashion. As noted there, I think this has to do with the separation of noxious liquid from beneficial liquid, a feat ascribed in natural terms to the sun and in mythological terms to Indra. When тАЬI fasten the poison on the sunтАЭ (p─Бda a), I am counting on the purificatory power of the sun to neutralize or banish the poison. This ritualistic action is matched in p─Бda b by fastening the skin onto the house of the sur─Б-possessor. Sur─Б is an alcoholic beverage of some sort (generally tr.

тАШBranntweinтАЩ, тАШbrandyтАЩ, et sim., though, acdg. to James McHugh [p.c.], it is unlikely that the technology of distilling was known to Vedic India, so probably some sort of beer; see now McHugh forthcoming [JAOS], тАЬThe Ancient Indian Alcoholic Drink Called Sur─Б: Vedic EvidenceтАЭ) and a universally condemned evil twin to soma, though it gets used in some ┼Ыrauta rituals, particularly the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л. The appearance of the sur─Б-possessor (s├║r─Бvant-) in b is owing to two factors: on the one hand, as just noted, sur─Б is a taboo drink and is therefore equivalent to the poison (viс╣г├б-) in p─Бda a. On the other, the word s├║r─Б- is phonologically reminiscent of тАШsunтАЩ s┼л╠Бrya- in p─Бda a.

The natural/ritual action depicted in the first p─Бda is, in my interpr., matched by the mythological action of the second p─Бda. I therefore do not take p─Бda b as a simile (as Geldner does), but as a parallel action – the attachment of a skin (dс╣Ы╠Бti-) full of poison/sur─Б on the house of the sur─Б-possessor, who, in my view, is Indra, who appears by epithet in p─Бda e. (Though Geldner and others tentatively identify hariс╣гс╣нh─Б╠Б- as the sun god, the тАШmounter of the fallow baysтАЩ can only be Indra.) Later Vedic has a cmpd. sur─Б-dс╣Ыti- тАШsur─Б-skinтАЩ, found in PB XIV.11.26 and JB III.229. Both passages concern the vip─Бnam of a liquid; vi тИЪp─Б, lit. тАШdrink apartтАЩ, is used for the separation of two kinds of liquids that have been mixed together (or separation of a liquid from something containing it); see comm. ad VII.22.4. In the late RV and later, this lexeme is specialized for the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л ritual, whose mythological foundation is the healing of Indra by the A┼Ыvins and Sarasvat─л, after he had drunk too much soma.

They make him drink sur─Б, which was mixed with soma (perhaps the soma he had already drunk), and he performs the feat of separating the two liquids. This myth is already present in X.131.4-5 with precisely this detail. When in p─Бda b here we fashion the skin of poison onto Indra the sur─Б-drinkerтАЩs house, we are implicitly asking him to perform the same feat for us. The refrain (found in vss. 10-13, p─Бdas c-f) makes it clear that he has succeeded. At least in my interpr., it is said that Indra has put the poison far in the distance (e) and the honeyed (plant?) has made honey (quite possibly soma, as often)(f): the two liquids have been separated and are separate, with the good one available to us. The result is that the mythological model, Indra, will not die (c) – nor will we (d) – and the poison with which we began has been rendered ineffective.

Griffith

I hang the poison in the Sun, a wine-skin in a vintner’s house,
He will not die, nor shall we die: his path is far: he whom Bay Horses bear hath turned thee to sweet meath.

Dem Sonnengott h├дnge ich das Gift auf wie einen Schlauch im Hause des Branntweinbesitzers. Er wird gewi├Я nicht daran sterben, noch werden wir sterben. Der Falbenlenker hat seine Verwendung beseitigt. Die s├╝├Яe Pflanze hat dich zu Honig gemacht.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThat little insignifcant bird has swallowed your venom; she does not die; nor shall we die; for, although afar off, yet drawn by his coursers, (the Sun) will overtake (the poison); the science of antidotes has converted you, (Poison), to ambrosia.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The insignificant bird: the feminine le kapi├▒jala, or francoline partridge, which was known as a remover of poison, viс╣гa hartr─л

Jamison Brereton

Such a little teeny ┼Ыakunti-birdтАФthat itty-bitty thing has eaten your poison.
Even now she will not die, and we will not die.
The mounter of the fallow bays [=Indra] has (made) its [=poisonтАЩs] trek far in the distance; the honeyed (plant) has made you honey.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The extraordinary density of -ka-suffixed forms begins here and lasts till the end of the hymn. That little birds eat the poison and destroy it may reflect the fact that many birds eat noxious insects without harm to them and with benefit to us. But the insects may no longer be the subject of this part of the hymn.

Griffith

This little bird, so very small, hath swallowed all thy poison up.
She will not die, nor shall we die: his path is far: he whom Bay Horses bear hath turned thee to sweet meath.

Dieses winzige V├╢gelchen, dies kleine hat dein Gift gefressen. Dies wird gewi├Я nicht daran sterben, noch werden wir sterben. Der Falbenlenker hat seine Verwendung beseitigt. Die s├╝├Яe Pflanze hat dich zu Honig gemacht.

Grassmann

Dies so winzige V├╢gelchen hat dein Gift verschlungen, und wird doch daran nicht sterben; auch wir werden nicht sterben u.s.w. (wie Vers 10.)

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the thrice-seven sparks (of Agni) consume the influence of the venom; they verily do not perish;nor shall we die; for, although afar off, the Sun, drawn by his coursers, will overtake the poison; the science of antidotes has converted you, (Poison), to ambrosia.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The thice seven sparks: the seven tongues, or flames of fire, may be multiplied as red, white and black; or vi┼Ыpuliс╣Еgak─Б = catik─Б, a feminine le sparrow of which there are 21 varieties, eaters of poison with impunity

Jamison Brereton

Three times seven, the little sparks [=small birds?] have swallowed the bloom of poison.
Even now they will not die, and we will not die.
The mounter of the fallow bays [=Indra] has (made) its [=poisonтАЩs] trek far in the distance; the honeyed (plant) has made you honey.

Jamison Brereton Notes

S─Бyaс╣Зa. suggests that the тАЬlittle sparksтАЭ (viс╣гpuliс╣Еgak├б-) are little sparrows.

This makes sense not only because of the birds in vss. 11 and 14, but because of the visual effect of flocks of small birds feeding: esp. when they are in bushes or underbrush they can burst up, out, and around at random almost like sparks. The viс╣гor course also recalls viс╣г├б- тАШpoisonтАЩ. I do not understand why there are 21 of them, save for the fact that thrice seven is a satisfying number. Similar numbers are found in the next two vss.

Griffith

The three-times-seven bright sparks of fire have swallowed up the poison’s strength.
They will not die, nor shall we die: his path is far: he whom Bay Horses bear hath turned thee to sweet meath.

Geldner

Die dreimal sieben F├╝nkchen haben die Blume des Giftes gefressen. Die sterben gewi├Я nicht daran, noch werden wir sterben. Der Falbenlenker hat seine Verwendung beseitigt. Die s├╝├Яe Pflanze hat dich zu Honig gemacht.

Grassmann

Die dreimal sieben Funkenspr├╝henden (?) haben die Essenz des Giftes verschlungen und werden doch daran nicht sterben, auch wir werden nicht sterben u.s.w. (wie Vers 10.)

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI recite the names of ninety and nine (rivers), the destroyers of poison; although afar off, (the Sun), drawn by his coursers, will overtake the poison; the science of antidotes has converted you, (Poison), to ambrosia.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Of the nine and ninety tormentors of poison,
I have mentioned the names of all.
The mounter of the fallow bays [=Indra] has (made) its [=poisonтАЩs] trek far in the distance; the honeyed (plant) has made you honey.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАЬtormentorsтАЭ (/harmers, destroyers) of poison, the hapax gen. pl.

r├│puс╣г─лс╣З─Бm, are feminine. The referent is entirely unclear, but the removers of poison in the next vs. are all feminine as well.

Griffith

Of ninety rivers and of nine with power to stay the venom’s course,–
The names of all I have secured: his path is far: he whom Bay Horses bear hath turned thee to sweet meath.

Geldner

Von den neunundneunzig Zerst├╢rerinnen des Giftes, von allen habe ich die Namen genannt. Der Falbenlenker hat seine Verwendung beseitigt. Die s├╝├Яe Pflanze hat dich zu Honig gemacht.

Grassmann

Ich habe die Essenz von allen neunundneunzig giftzerst├╢renden Pflanzen genommen; der auf goldfarbenem Rosse reitende [Sonnengott] trieb weithin sein Gespann und dich [o Gift] hat er in s├╝ssen Honig verwandelt.

Elizarenkova

рддреНрд░рд┐рдГ рд╕рдкреНрдд рдПрдХрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рддрд┐рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдГ рдордпреВрд░реНрдпрдГ рдордпреВрд░рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдГ ред рддрд╛ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдХрд╛рд░рд┐рд╕рд░реНрдкрджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рд┐рдгреНрдпрдГ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдГ рдирд╛рдЧрджреНрд╡реЗрд╖рд┐рдЧрд░реБрдбрдкрдХреНрд╖рд╛рджреБрддреНрдкрдиреНрдирддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ред рддрдерд╛ рд╕рдкреНрдд рдПрддрд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рдХрд╛рдГ рд╕рд░реНрдкрдгрд╕реНрд╡рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕рд╛рд░рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдореЗрд╡ рд╕рд░рдгрд╛рдГ рдЕрдЧреНрд░реБрд╡рдГ ред рдирджреАрдирд╛рдореИрддрддреН ред рд╕реБрд░рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд╛рдГ рд╕рдкреНрдд рдирджреНрдпрдГ рд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рддрд╛рд╕реНрддреЗ рд╣реЗ рджреЗрд╣ рддрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдВ рд╡рд┐ рдЬрднреНрд░рд┐рд░реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рд╣рд░рдиреНрддреБ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рдЙрджрдХрдВ рдХреБрдореНрднрд┐рдиреАрдГ рдХреБрдореНрднрд┐рдиреНрдпрдГ рдХреБрдореНрднрд╡рддреНрдпрдГ рдХреБрдореНрднреЗрди рдЬрд▓рд╣рд╛рд░рд┐рдгреНрдпрдГ рдЗрд╡ ред рддрд╛ рдпрдерд╛ рддрджреНрдзрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдирджреНрдпреЛ рдордпреВрд░реНрдпрд╢реНрдЪ рдЕрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рднреВрддрдВ рд╣рд░рдиреНрддреБ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the thrice-seven peahens, the seven-sister rivers, carry off, (O Body), your poison, as maidens, with pitchers, carry away water.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Thrice-seven peahen: tri saptamay┼лryaс╕е, an allusion to the enmity between peafowl and snakes; 21 varities of mayur─л or peahen; the seven rivers are those of heaven, or the branches of the divine gaс╣Еg─Б; all running streams are possibly regarded as antidotes

Jamison Brereton

The three-times-seven peahens, the seven spinster sisters,
these have carried away your poison, like women with jugs
(carrying) water.

Griffith

So have the peahens three-times-seven, so have the maiden Sisters Seven
Carried thy venom far away, as girls bear water in their jars.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the insignificant mongoose (carry off) your venom, (Poison); if not, I will crush the vile (creature) with a stone; so may the poison depart (from my body) and go to distant regions.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The mongoose: kuс╣гumbako nakulaс╕е, the mongoose, whose hostility to the snake is proverbial

Jamison Brereton

Such a little teeny kuс╣гumbha-bugтАФI split that itty-bitty thing with a rock.
Thence has the poison rolled forth, following channels facing away (from us). с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The -ka- suffix is particularly prominent in these vss, appearing not only on the designation of the bug (kuс╣гumbhak├бс╕е, 2x), but also on the pronominal adj.

iyattak├бс╕е (тАШsuch a oneтАЩ), the pronoun tak├бm, and the participle pravartam─Бnak├бс╕е.

The word for тАШscorpionтАЩ, vс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыcika- only appears in that form, but appears to contain the -ka- suffix as well, very common in words for noxious insects (see my тАЬ-kasuffix,тАЭ IIJ 52 [2009]: 318).

Griffith

The poison-insect is so small; I crush the creature with a stone.
I turn the poison hence away, departed unto distant lands.

Geldner

Gar winzig ist der Kusumbhaka; den kleinen zerschlage ich mit dem Steine. Daraus ist das Gift fortgegangen in den von uns abgewandten Richtungen.

Grassmann

So winzig das Giftinsekt ist, so klein es ist, ich zerschlage es mit dem Steine, davon ist das Gift weggewandt in ferne Gegenden hin.

Elizarenkova

тАЬHastening forth at the command (of Agastya), thus spoke the mongoose: the venom of the scorpion is innocuous; scorpion, your venom is innocuous.тАЭ

тАЬWithout juice is the poison of the little scorpion, without juice is your poison, little scorpion.тАЭ с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

The -ka- suffix is particularly prominent in these vss, appearing not only on the designation of the bug (kuс╣гumbhak├бс╕е, 2x), but also on the pronominal adj.

iyattak├бс╕е (тАШsuch a oneтАЩ), the pronoun tak├бm, and the participle pravartam─Бnak├бс╕е.

The word for тАШscorpionтАЩ, vс╣Ы╠Б┼Ыcika- only appears in that form, but appears to contain the -ka- suffix as well, very common in words for noxious insects (see my тАЬ-kasuffix,тАЭ IIJ 52 [2009]: 318).

Griffith

Forth issuing from the mountain’s side the poison-insect spake and said:
Scorpion, they venom is but weak.

Geldner

Kusumbhaka sprach also, da er vom Gebirge ausging: “Kraftlos ist das Gift des Skorpions, kraftlos ist dein Gift du Skorpion.

Grassmann

Das winzige Giftinsekt, als es vom Berge herab sich wandte, sprach dies Wort: Das Gift des Skorpions ist wirkungslos, dein Gift, o Skorpion, ist wirkungslos.

Elizarenkova

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдЧрд┐рд░реЗрдГ) рдкрд░реНрд╡рдд рд╕реЗ (рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирдХрдГ) рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ (рдХреБрд╖реБрдореНрднрдХрдГ) рдЫреЛрдЯрд╛ рдиреЗрдЙрд▓рд╛ (рд╡реГрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХрд╕реНрдп) рд╡реАрдЫреА рдХреЗ (рд╡рд┐рд╖рдореН) рд╡рд┐рд╖ рдХреЛ (рдЕрд░рд╕рдореН) рдиреАрд░рд╕ рдЬреЛ (рдЕрдмреНрд░рд╡реАрддреН) рдХрд╣рддрд╛ рдЕрд░реНрдерд╛рддреН рдЪреЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рд╕реЗ рджреВрд╕рд░реЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬрддрд╛рддрд╛ рд╣реИ (рддрддреН) рдЗрд╕ рдХрд╛рд░рдг рд╣реЗ (рд╡реГрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХ) рдЕрдЩреНрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЫреЗрджрди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреА (рддреЗ) рддреЗрд░реЗ (рдЕрд░рд╕рдореН) рдЕрд░рд╕ (рд╡рд┐рд╖рдореН) рд╡рд┐рд╖ рд╣реИ рее резрем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рд╡реАрдЫреА рдЖрджрд┐ рдЫреЛрдЯреЗ-рдЫреЛрдЯреЗ рдЬреАрд╡реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖ рд╣рд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддреАрдп рдирд┐рдЙрд▓реЗ рдХрд╛ рд╕рдВрд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░реЗрдВ, рдЬрд┐рд╕рд╕реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖-рд░реЛрдЧреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдореЗрдВ рд╕рдорд░реНрде рд╣реЛрд╡реЗрдВ рее резрем реердЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╖ рд╣рд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реА рдУрд╖рдзреА, рд╡рд┐рд╖ рд╣рд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЬреАрд╡ рдФрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╣рд╛рд░реА рд╡реЗрджреНрдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдг рдХрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрди рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рдЗрд╕ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдХреЗ рдЕрд░реНрде рдХреА рдкрд┐рдЫрд▓реЗ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрде рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐ рд╣реИ, рдпрд╣ рд╕рдордЭрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реердпрд╣ рдПрдХрд╕реМ рдПрдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд╡рд╛рдБ рд╕реВрдХреНрдд рдФрд░ рд╕реЛрд▓рд╣рд╡рд╛рдБ рд╡рд░реНрдЧ рдЪреМрдмреАрд╕рд╡рд╛рдБ рдЕрдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХ рдФрд░ рдкреНрд░рдердо рдордгреНрдбрд▓ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реБрдЖ реередрдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрдорддреНрдкрд░рдорд╣рдВрд╕рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реНрд░рд╛рдЬрдХрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдкрд░рдорд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╡рд┐рд░рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрджрд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреАрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирд╛рдВ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпреЗрдг рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджреНрджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреАрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрд╛рд░реНрдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рдордиреНрд╡рд┐рддреЗ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрдпреБрдХреНрддреЗ рд╕реБрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рд╡рд┐рднреВрд╖рд┐рддреЗ рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрджрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рдордгреНрдбрд▓рдВ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдореН рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдЧрд┐рд░реЗрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирдХрдГ рдХреБрд╖реБрдореНрднрдХреЛ рд╡реГрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рд╖рдорд░рд╕рдВ рдпрджрдмреНрд░рд╡реАрддреНрддрддреНрддрддреЛ рд╣реЗ рд╡реГрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХ рддреЗрд╜рд░рд╕рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдорд╕реНрддрд┐ рее резрем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрде рд╡реГрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХрд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╣рд░рдгрд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдорд╛рд╣ ред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдХреБрд╖реБрдореНрднрдХрдГ) рдЕрд▓реНрдкрдГ рдХреБрд╖реБрдореНрднреЛ рдирдХреБрд▓рдГ (рддрддреН) (рдЕрдмреНрд░рд╡реАрддреН) рдмреНрд░реВрддреЗ (рдЧрд┐рд░реЗрдГ) рд╢реИрд▓рд╛рддреН (рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирдХрдГ) рдкреНрд░рдХреГрд╖реНрдЯрддрдпрд╛ рд╡рд░реНрддреНрддрдорд╛рдирдГ (рд╡реГрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХрд╕реНрдп) (рдЕрд░рд╕рдореН) рдЕрд╡рд┐рджреНрдпрд╛рдорд╛рдирд░рд╕рдореН (рд╡рд┐рд╖рдореН) (рдЕрд░рд╕рдореН) (рд╡реГрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХрдГ) рдпреЛ рд╡реГрд╢реНрдЪрддрд┐ рдЫрд┐рдирддреНрддреНрдпрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирд┐ рддрд╕реНрдп (рддреЗ) рддрд╕реНрдп (рд╡рд┐рд╖рдореН) рее резрем рее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрд╛ рд╡реГрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХрд╛рджрд┐рд╡рд┐рд╖рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдХрдВ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддреАрдпрдирдХреБрд▓рд╕рдВрд░рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпреБрд░реНрдпрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╖рд░реЛрдЧрдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдгрдХреНрд╖рдорд╛ рднрд╡реЗрдпреБрд░рд┐рддрд┐ рее резрем рее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╣рд░реМрд╖рдзрдЬреАрд╡рд╡рд┐рд╖рд╡реИрджреНрдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджреНрдпрдореН реердЗрддрд┐ рдПрдХрдирд╡рддреНрдпреБрддреНрддрд░рдВ рд╢рддрддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖реЛрдбрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд░реНрд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрдГ рдкреНрд░рдердордВ рдордгреНрдбрд▓рдЮреНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдорд╛рдгрд╕рд╛рдВрдиреА рд╡реГрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдХ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреАрдЪреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖ рдирд╖реНрдЯ рдХрд░рдгрд╛рд▒реНрдпрд╛ рдкрд░реНрд╡рддреАрдп рдореБрдВрдЧреБрд╕ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреЗ рд╕рдВрд░рдХреНрд╖рдг рдХрд░рд╛рд╡реЗ. рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рд╡рд┐рд╖ рд░реЛрдЧрд╛рдЪреЗ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд░рдг рдХрд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рд╕ рддреЗ рд╕рдорд░реНрде рд╡реНрд╣рд╛рд╡реЗрдд. рее резрем рее
